<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This letter reports the design and experimental evaluation of three compact printed monopole antennas for UHF RFID applications. The antennas that include folded, 2-D meander, and 3-D meander monopole designs are inductively coupled to RFID chips and are fabricated using a 1.524-mm-thick Rogers RB4350B substrate with the relative permittivity of 3.66. Experimental results reveal that these tags cover the worldwide UHF RFID operation band (860-960 MHz) with a maximum readable range of 6.3 m for the folded monopole, 5.39 m for the 2-D meander, and 5.24 m for the 3-D meander monopole designs with an effective isotropic radiated power of 3.28 W. A method for measuring the radiation pattern of an assembled UHF RFID tag without the use of any additional matching circuits or feeding wires is presented. This method is used to measure the radiation pattern of the fabricated 3-D meander monopole tag antenna.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

The RFID tag, which is affixed to the objects to be identified, is composed of an RFID chip and an antenna. The tag antenna plays an important role in the overall RFID system performance, as it directly impacts the size, cost, and detection range. From the measured results of the required minimum (threshold) power for creating a correct tag response at each frequency point in the selected bandwidth, the reading range of the tag can be found using the following formula [3]:  where \\$d\\$ is the distance between the tag under test and the transmitter antenna of the measurement system. \\${P}_{\\min}\\$ is the minimum transmit power obtained from the measurement system for generating a correct tag response, \\${G}_{\\rm t}\\$ is the gain of TX antenna, \\${L}_{\\rm c}\\$ is the loss in the connection cable, and \\${P}_{\\rm EIRP}\\$ is the allowed maximum transmit power that is determined by the EIRP of 3.28 W, (ERP 2 W) which is recommended by the European Telecommunications Standards Institute (ETSI) [3].&quot;,&quot;part&quot;:&quot;1&quot;},{&quot;sec&quot;:&quot;sec3&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot; We discuss various requirements of such designs, outline a generic design process including range measurement techniques and concentrate on one practical application: RFID tag for box tracking in warehouses. A loaded meander antenna design for this application is described and its various practical aspects such as sensitivity to fabrication process and box content are analyzed. <div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>The radio frequency identification (RFID) field has received considerable attention recently due to the growing number, as well as the variety, of applications it supports. This is in particular true for the ultrahigh frequency band (UHF) RFID services, which are now reaching beyond supply chain management and tracking to electronic payment and mobile phones <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. In RFID applications, it is strongly desired to maintain a minimal footprint for the tag. This makes the tag antenna design at the UHF band more critical since the small radiating aperture area could compromise the antenna gain and hence the reading range. Besides the size constraint and gain requirement, the design challenges of RFID tag antennas include matching to the RFID chip and achieving wideband operation in order to secure a global market rather than a specific country. In an earlier work by the authors, a few compact printed monopole antennas with inductive coupling feed systems were designed for passive UHF RFID tag applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. However, experimental evaluations of the assembled tags, in which the chip is connected to the antenna, remained to be completed.</p><p>To evaluate the performance of an assembled RFID tag, parameters such as power sensitivity, radar cross section, and reading range as a function of operating frequency are measured often using the techniques presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. To measure the radiation pattern of tag antennas, matching circuits and feeding wires are necessary when a conventional radiation pattern measurement system is used <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. These additional components, which do not exist when the tag is deployed, influence the radiation pattern. A contactless method in which the feeding wires are removed is introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> in order to replicate a tag's operation in practice. In this type of test, two tones are transmitted to the tag, and the third-order intermodulation products that are generated by the nonlinear IC of the tag are detected <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. The amplitude of an intermodulation product is proportional to the nonlinear characteristics of the RFID chip, the amplitudes of the fundamental frequencies, and also to the gain of tag antenna. Therefore, the radiation pattern can be obtained by plotting the normalized amplitude of the received intermodulation product. The drawback of this method, in addition to the increased complexity of the test setup, is its dependence on the sensitivity of the receiver. The RFID reader system can also be used to plot the radiation pattern of an assembled tag by sweeping the transmitter power of the reader and measuring the minimum power required to activate the tag at each angle <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Like the previous method, the measured pattern is also a function of reader (receiver) sensitivity.</p><p>In this letter, the new tag antennas introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a> are revised and fabricated for integration with a chip having the input impedance of 8.2-j61 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. A simple method to measure the radiation pattern of passive RFID tag antennas using a vector network analyzer and by determining a calibrated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also proposed. The radiation pattern of the 3-D meander monopole tag antenna, which offers the smallest footprint among the designed tag antennas, while connected to a commercially available microchip is measured using the proposed method. To fully evaluate the fabricated tags, the minimum required power for chip activation, the differential radar cross section, and the reading range are also measured across the frequency band of 800â1000 MHz. Measurements of the power sensitivity and reading range indicate that the proposed tags operate efficiently across the whole UHF frequency band of 860â960 MHz. It is found that the maximum reading range of the designed 3-D meander monopole tag is 5.24 m, which is comparable to the values reported for planar meander dipole antennas while taking a notably smaller area.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Proposed Tag Antenna Designs</h2></div><p>The compact printed monopole antennas that were introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2">[2]</a> are redesigned and fabricated using a 1.524-mm-thick Rogers RO4350B substrate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-13" role="math" style="width: 5.348em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.808em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.69em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Îµ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">3.66</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">(\varepsilon_{\rm r}=3.66)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The structure and the dimensions of the proposed printed folded monopole antenna are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. The overall area is 63Ã24 mm<sup>2</sup>, which is relatively small compared to the conventional folded dipole presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a> as the area is reduced by 64%. For maximum power transfer to the RFID chip, an inductively coupled loop matching mechanism is utilized for the antenna. As explained in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2">[2]</a>, meander monopole antennas are developed to further reduce the size of UHF RFID tags. Two meander monopole antenna topologies are designed and fabricated. The geometry of the printed 2-D meander monopole antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(a)</a>. Like a folded monopole antenna, the radiating body, the feeding loop, and the ground are printed on the top layer of the substrate. The overall size of the designed antenna is (42Ã25.7 mm<sup>2</sup>), which is 28% smaller than the folded monopole design shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. In comparison to a pertinent meander dipole design reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_2">[3]</a>, an overall 33% area reduction is achieved. The 3-D meander monopole antenna structure is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(b)</a>, in which conductor traces are implemented on both sides of the substrate and connected using vias, each with a radius of 0.381 mm. A matching loop is also used to feed the 3-D meander monopole antenna. Like the folded monopole antenna, the dimensions of the matching printed loop and its spacing from the antenna are adjusted to yield the desired impedance values <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2">[2]</a>. The overall size of the 3-D meander antennas is (42Ã19.7 mm<sup>2</sup>) or equivalently <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-24" role="math" style="width: 8.111em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.27em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1007.15em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.128</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">0.06</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">(0.128\lambda\times 0.06\lambda)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The 3-D meander monopole antenna offers the smallest area, which is 45% and 23.4% smaller than the folded and 2-D meander monopole antennas, respectively, while offering almost similar performance characteristics, as will be seen in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>. When compared to the dimensions of the compact tags reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>, the proposed 3-D meander monopole tag has 39.8%â82% less surface area.

display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.715em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.65em 2.45em -999.997em); overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">{\rm d}2=6</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-263" role="math" style="width: 4.368em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.442em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1003.44em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-264"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-265"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-266"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-267" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-268" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-269" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-270" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">3.4</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">{\rm d}3=3.4</script></tex-math></inline-formula>).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6151802/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The designed tag antennas are each integrated with a chip that has an input impedance of 8.2-j61 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-271" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-272"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-273" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the operation frequency of 915 MHz. The simulated input impedance results are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>. Finding the impedance values at the operation frequency of 915 MHz, one can calculate the realized gain of the folded, 2-D meander, and 3-D meander monopole antennas, which are 1.7, 0.85, and 0.91 dB, respectively. The general formulation to obtain the realized gain of an RFID tag antenna can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>. Also, the simulated radiation efficiency of the folded monopole is 94.7%, while 78.4% is observed for the 2-D and 78.93% for the 3-D meander monopole antennas.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Input impedance of the proposed folded, 2-D meander, and 3-D meander monopole antennas.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6151802/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Experimental Evaluations of the Proposed Tags</h2></div><p>To fully evaluate an RFID tag radiation pattern, the required minimum power on the tag, the differential radar cross section <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-274" role="math" style="width: 4.027em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.607em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.49em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-276" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-277" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-278"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-279"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-280" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-281" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-283" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">(\Delta{\rm RCS})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the reading range should be measured.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Proposed measurements setup.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6151802/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><i>Radiation Pattern</i>: Passive UHF RFID tags do not contain an internal power source for their microchip, and they generate their needed power from the RF signal received by the tag antenna. Therefore, radiation pattern characterization of the tag antenna is critical in evaluating the performance of an RFID tag since it provides a visualization of the incident power on the tag. The proposed system for radiation pattern measurement of passive UHF RFID tags is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. This measurement setup includes a vector network analyzer, two horn antennas, and an amplifier. Port 1 of the VNA is connected to the power amplifier to generate 30 dBm, and then to the transmitter (TX with gain of 6 dBi) antenna. The transmitter antenna is placed close to the RFID tag under test (at 0.69 m distance, which is in the far-field region of the antenna) to activate the RFID chip. Accounting for propagation losses, the power received by the RFID antenna is 8 dBm, which is higher than the minimum power required (â13 dBm). Both the RFID holder and the transmitter(TX) are mounted on the turntable of the anechoic chamber to ensure a continuous illumination field for the tag under test. The receiver (RX) antenna is connected to Port 2 of the VNA to measure <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-284" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-287"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-288"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-289" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-291"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-292" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The tag is placed on a foam substrate as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>, and the distance between the RX antenna and the RFID tag is 1.84 m. Radiation pattern of the fabricated 3-D meander monopole antenna with the microchip was measured using this setup in an anechoic chamber. The first step in this measurement is calibration in order to account for the reflections inside the chamber such as those reflected from the chamber walls or from the holder to which the tag is attached. This is done by measuring <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-293" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-294"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-295"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-296"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-298" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> across the selected frequency band when no RFID tag is present. This test is repeated at each angle of the turntable from 0Â° to 360Â° stepped by 5Â°. The measured value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-302" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-304"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-305"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-306"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-307" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-308"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-309"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-310" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at each angle includes the internal reflection inside the anechoic chamber, which is used as a calibrating reference. Next, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-311" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-312"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-313"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-315"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-318"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is measured again at each angle in the presence of the RFID tag. The reference <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-320" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-321"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-323"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-324"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-325" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-327"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-328" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values are subtracted from these new measured values to find the received (a.k.a. return) signal from the RFID tag. The radiation pattern of the RFID tag can then be obtained simply by plotting the normalized measured return signals at each frequency point in the selected bandwidth. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> presents the simulated and measured radiation patterns at the operation frequency of 915 MHz. The measured half-power beamwidth is 82Â°. The radiation patterns are omnidirectional and similar to those of dipole antennas. The radiation pattern characteristics of the two other designed antennas are very close to those of the 3-D meander monopole. Hence, these radiation plots are not presented in this letter for brevity.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>Radiation pattern at 915 MHz of the 3-D meander tag. (a) Simulated 3-D radiation pattern. (b) Measured and simulated 2-D radiation pattern.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6151802/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><i>Power sensitivity</i>: The proposed folded, 2-D meander, and 3-D meander RFID tags were measured in an anechoic cabinet designed for evaluating the performance of UHF RFID tags at Voyantic Ltd.'s laboratory <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3">[15]</a>. The transmitter and receiver antennas in this measurement system are linearly polarized, providing a flat 8-dBi gain response at the frequency range of 800â1000 MHz. The measurement system also includes a wideband circulator for monostatic radar measurements with over 20 dB port isolation throughout the 800â1000-MHz range. The circulator is connected to an RFID tester that generated query commands with selected modulation, data rate, and encoding formats for UHF tags operating under ISO 18000-6c (EPC Class 1 Gen2) protocol. The power sensitivity of the RFID tag is measured by sweeping the transmit power across the selected frequency band to detect the minimum power required to obtain a correct tag response at each frequency point. The transmit power starts from a value to which the tag does not respond, and then it is increased by 0.1-dB steps until a correct response is obtained. The maximum power generated by the transmitter system is 27 dBm. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a> presents the results of the required minimum transmit (also referred to as threshold) power on the tag in the forward link. In calculation of these values, the gain of the transmitter antenna, which is 8 dB, and the calculated free-space path loss of 23 dB are considered to obtain the power on the tag. These results demonstrate that the tags respond correctly across the entire frequency band of 800â1000 MHz when at most 3.28 W of effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) is incident on the tag.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Minimum required transmit power on the tag for generating the correct tag response.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6151802/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><i>Radar Cross Section</i>: The minimum power needed for identifying the tag in radar terminology translates into the strength of the backscattered signal at the reader. Therefore, the differential radar cross section <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-329" role="math" style="width: 4.027em; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">(\Delta{\rm RCS})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which determines the ratio of the backscattered power from the tag to the incoming power sent by the transmitter, is also obtained from the following formula for the monostatic radar measurement configuration <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_3">[4]</a>: <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-339" role="math" style="width: 100%; The tag is vertically positioned on the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-445" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; The results of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-453" role="math" style="width: 3.126em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.826em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.77em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-454"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-455" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-456"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-457"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-458" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-459" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-460" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">\Delta{\rm RCS}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as a function of frequency of the proposed tags are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. The peak measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-461" role="math" style="width: 3.126em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.826em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.77em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-462"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-463" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-464"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-465"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-466" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-467" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-468" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\Delta{\rm RCS}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the folded monopole and the 2-D and 3D meander monopole RFID tags are (â21.9 dBsqm) and (â30.66 dBsqm) and (â30.32 dBsqm), respectively. A tag with a strong response can be easily detected by a reader and, as expected, the folded monopole tag with the largest physical area creates the strongest response of the three designed antennas.

<p></p><p><i>Reading Range</i>: The most common and probably the most important indicator in evaluating an RFID tag is its reading range. From the measured results of the required minimum (threshold) power for creating a correct tag response at each frequency point in the selected bandwidth, the reading range of the tag can be found using the following formula <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3">[3]</a>: <disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-479" role="math" style="width: 100%; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">{P}_{\min}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the minimum transmit power obtained from the measurement system for generating a correct tag response, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-539" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-540"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-541"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-542"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-543"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-544" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-545"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-546"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-547" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">{G}_{\rm t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of TX antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-548" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-549"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-550"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-553" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-554"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-556" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">{L}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the loss in the connection cable, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-557" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.47em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-558"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-559"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-560"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-561"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-562" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-564"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-565" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">E</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-566" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-567" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-568" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">P</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">{P}_{\rm EIRP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the allowed maximum transmit power that is determined by the EIRP of 3.28 W, (ERP 2 W) which is recommended by the European Telecommunications Standards Institute (ETSI) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3">[3]</a>. For other countries that allow 4 W EIRP, a 10.43% should be added to the reading range results. The maximum reading range for each of the proposed RFID tags versus the frequency over the 800â1000-MHz band is presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>. It can be observed that the proposed RFID tags are functional across the entire UHF frequency band of 860â960 MHz. The maximum readable ranges of the folded, 2-D meander, and 3-D meander monopole tags are 6.38, 5.39, and 5.24 m, respectively, with an EIRP of 3.28 W, which are superior to the maximum reading of comparable antenna topologies such as the meander dipole tag antenna presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3">[3]</a> with the reading range of 5 m.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6151802/6151802-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 8. </b><fig><p>Reading ranges of the proposed tags as a function of frequency.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6151802/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>Three compact printed monopole antennas are fabricated for use in UHF RFID tags that contain a chip with an input impedance of 8.2-j61 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-569" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-570"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-571" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. A method for measuring the radiation pattern of the passive RFID tag was presented using a network analyzer and by determining a calibrated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-572" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-573"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-574"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-575"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-576"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-577" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-578"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">{S}_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Using the proposed method, the radiation pattern of an assembled tag antenna including the chip can be measured without any probes or cables directly connected to the antenna. This is important as it represents how the tag is used in practice. The radiation pattern of the prototyped 3-D meander monopole tag was measured showing an omnidirectional shape similar to that of a conventional dipole antenna. The power sensitivity of the designed RFID tags was also measured by sweeping the power source and determining the minimum power level needed for generating a correct response to a command. The experimental results also demonstrated that the maximum readable range of the proposed folded, 2-D meander, and 3-D meander monopole tags are 6.38, 5.39, and 5.24 m, respectively, with an EIRP of 3.28 W. The proposed RFID tags are functional across the worldwide UHF band, thus offering a compact, inexpensive, and efficient solution for passive UHF RFID tags that can be marketed globally for a variety of applications.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank J. Partanen at the VoyanticLtd. laboratory for conducting power sensitivity, RCS, and reading range tag measurements.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
